          </msqrt>\n               </mfrac>\n              </mrow>\n             </mstyle>\n            </mrow>\n            <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\n             {\\displaystyle \\gamma ={\\frac {1}{\\sqrt {1-v^{2}/c^{2}}}}}\n            </annotation>\n           </semantics>\n          </math>\n         </span>\n         <img alt="\\gamma ={\\frac {1}{\\sqrt {1-v^{2}/c^{2}}}}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/8b130ec5e5e9586833b7888f7cbe2433f1e295e3" style="vertical-align: -3.338ex; width:17.027ex; height:6.676ex;"/>\n        </span>\n       </dd>\n      </dl>\n      <p>\n       The invariant mass of systems is the same for observers in all inertial frames, while the relativistic mass depends on the observer\'s\n       <a href="/wiki/Frame_of_reference" title="Frame of reference">\n        frame of reference\n       </a>\n       . In order to formulate the equations of physics such that mass values do not change between observers, it is convenient to use rest mass. The rest mass of a body is also related to its energy\n       <i>\n        E\n       </i>\n       and the magnitude of its momentum\n       <b>\n        p\n       </b>\n       by the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Relativistic_energy-momentum_equation" title="Relativistic energy-momentum equation">\n        relativistic energy-momentum equation\n       </a>\n       :\n      </p>\n      <dl>\n       <dd>\n        <span class="mwe-math-element">\n         <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">\n          <math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n           <semantics>\n            <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n             <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n              <mo stretchy="false">\n               (\n              </mo>\n              <msub>\n               <mi>\n                m\n               </mi>\n               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n                <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n                 <mi mathvariant="normal">\n                  r\n                 </mi>\n                 <mi mathvariant="normal">\n                  e\n                 </mi>\n                 <mi mathvariant="normal">\n                  s\n                 </mi>\n                 <mi mathvariant="normal">\n                  t\n                 </mi>\n                </mrow>\n               </mrow>\n              </msub>\n              <mo stretchy="false">\n               )\n              </mo>\n              <msup>\n               <mi>\n                c\n               </mi>\n               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n                <mn>\n                 2\n                </mn>\n               </mrow>\n              </msup>\n              <mo>\n               =\n              </mo>\n              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n               <msqrt>\n                <msubsup>\n                 <mi>\n                  E\n                 </mi>\n                 <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n                  <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n                   <mi mathvariant="normal">\n                    t\n                   </mi>\n                   <mi mathvariant="normal">\n                    o\n                   </mi>\n                   <mi mathvariant="normal">\n                    t\n                   </mi>\n                   <mi mathvariant="normal">\n                    a\n                   </mi>\n                   <mi mathvariant="normal">\n                    l\n                   </mi>\n                  </mrow>\n                 </mrow>\n                 <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n                  <mn>\n                   2\n                  </mn>\n                 </mrow>\n                </msubsup>\n                <mo>\n                 \xe2\x88\x92\n                 <!-- \xe2\x88\x92 -->\n                </mo>\n                <mo stretchy="false">\n                 (\n                </mo>\n                <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n                 <mo stretchy="false">\n                  |\n                 </mo>\n                </mrow>\n                <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n                 <mi mathvariant="bold">\n                  p\n                 </mi>\n                </mrow>\n                <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n                 <mo stretchy="false">\n                  |\n                 </mo>\n                </mrow>\n                <mi>\n                 c\n                </mi>\n                <msup>\n                 <mo stretchy="false">\n                  )\n                 </mo>\n                 <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n                  <mn>\n                   2\n                  </mn>\n                 </mrow>\n                </msup>\n               </msqrt>\n              </mrow>\n              <mo>\n               .\n              </mo>\n              <mspace width="negativethinmathspace">\n              </mspace>\n             </mstyle>\n            </mrow>\n            <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\n             {\\displaystyle (m_{\\mathrm {rest} })c^{2}={\\sqrt {E_{\\mathrm {total} }^{2}-(|\\mathbf {p} |c)^{2}}}.\\!}\n            </annotation>\n           </semantics>\n          </math>\n         </span>\n         <img alt="(m_{\\mathrm {rest} })c^{2}={\\sqrt {E_{\\mathrm {total} }^{2}-(|\\mathbf {p} |c)^{2}}}.\\!" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/79c389672f3df92524d4cdb0e4510f22af1f51d2" style="vertical-align: -1.838ex; margin-right: -0.204ex; width:29.747ex; height:4.843ex;"/>\n        </span>\n       </dd>\n      </dl>\n      <p>\n       So long as the system is\n       <a href="/wiki/Closed_system" title="Closed system">\n        closed\n       </a>\n       with respect to mass and energy, both kinds of mass are conserved in any given frame of reference. The conservation of mass holds even as some types of particles are converted to others. Matter particles (such as atoms) may be converted to non-matter particles (such as photons of light), but this does not affect the total amount of mass or energy. Although things like heat may not be matter, all types of energy still continue to exhibit mass.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34">\n        <a href="#cite_note-34">\n         [note 9]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35">\n        <a href="#cite_note-35">\n         [26]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Thus, mass and energy do not change into one another in relativity; rather, both are names for the same thing, and neither mass nor energy\n       <i>\n        appear\n       </i>\n       without the other.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Both rest and relativistic mass can be expressed as an energy by applying the well-known relationship\n       <a href="/wiki/Mass%E2%80%93energy_equivalence" title="Mass\xe2\x80\x93energy equivalence">\n        <i>\n         E\n        </i>\n        =\n        <i>\n         mc\n        </i>\n        <sup>\n         2\n        </sup>\n       </a>\n       , yielding\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rest_energy" title="Rest energy">\n        rest energy\n       </a>\n       and "relativistic energy" (total system energy) respectively:\n      </p>\n      <dl>\n       <dd>\n        <span class="mwe-math-element">\n         <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">\n          <math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n           <semantics>\n            <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n             <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n              <msub>\n           =\n              </mo>\n              <mo stretchy="false">\n               (\n              </mo>\n              <msub>\n               <mi>\n                m\n               </mi>\n               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n                <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n                 <mi mathvariant="normal">\n                  r\n                 </mi>\n                 <mi         </mo>\n              <msup>\n               <mi>\n                c\n               </mi>\n               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n                <mn>\n                 2\n    </span>\n       </dd>\n       <dd>\n        <span class="mwe-math-element">\n         <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">\n          <math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n           <semantics>\n            <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n             <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n              <msub>\n               <mi>\n                E\n               </mi>\n               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n                <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n                 <mi mathvariant="normal">\n         </mi>\n                 <mi mathvariant="normal">\n                  a\n                 </mi>\n                 <mi mathvariant="normal">\n                  l\n                 </mi>\n                </mrow>\n               </mrow>\n              </msub>\n              <mo>\n               =\n              </mo>\n              <mo stretchy="false">\n               (\n              </mo>\n              <msub>\n               <mi>\n                m\n               </mi>\n               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n                <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n                 <mi mathvariant="normal">\n                  r\n                 </mi>\n                 <mi mathvariant="normal">\n                  e\n                 </mi>\n                 <mi mathvariant="normal">\n                  l\n                 </mi>\n                 <mi mathvariant="normal">\n                  a\n                 </mi>\n                 <mi mathvariant="normal">\n                  t\n                 </mi>\n                 <mi mathvariant="normal">\n                  i\n                 </mi>\n                 <mi mathvariant="normal">\n                  v\n                 </mi>\n                 <mi mathvariant="normal">\n                  e\n                 </mi>\n                </mrow>\n               </mrow>\n              </msub>\n              <mo stretchy="false">\n               )\n              </mo>\n              <msup>\n               <mi>\n                c\n               </mi>\n               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n                <mn>\n                 2\n                </mn>\n               </mrow>\n              </msup>\n              <mspace width="negativethinmathspace">\n              </mspace>\n             </mstyle>\n            </mrow>\n            <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\n             {\\displaystyle E_{\\mathrm {total} }=(m_{\\mathrm {relative} })c^{2}\\!}\n            </annotation>\n           </semantics>\n          </math>\n         </span>\n         <img alt="E_{\\mathrm {total} }=(m_{\\mathrm {relative} })c^{2}\\!" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/c94f0618c9b572603532107afb1651ac1e446bc7" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; margin-right: -0.387ex; width:20.085ex; height:3.176ex;"/>\n        </span>\n       </dd>\n      </dl>\n      <p>\n       The "relativistic" mass and energy concepts are related to their "rest" counterparts, but they do not have the same value as their rest counterparts in systems where there is a net momentum. Because the relativistic mass is\n       <a href="/wiki/Mass%E2%80%93energy_equivalence" title="Mass\xe2\x80\x93energy equivalence">\n        proportional to the energy\n       </a>\n       , it has gradually fallen into disuse among physicists.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36">\n        <a href="#cite_note-36">\n         [27]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       There is disagreement over whether the concept remains useful\n       <a href="/wiki/Pedagogy" title="Pedagogy">\n        pedagogically\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-okun_37-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-okun-37">\n         [28]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38">\n        <a href="#cite_note-38">\n         [29]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39">\n        <a href="#cite_note-39">\n         [30]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In bound systems, the\n       <a href="/wiki/Binding_energy" title="Binding energy">\n        binding energy\n       </a>\n       must often be subtracted from the mass of the unbound system, because binding energy commonly leaves the system at the time it is bound. The mass of the system changes in this process merely because the system was not closed during the binding process, so the energy escaped. For example, the binding energy of\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Atomic_nuclei" title="Atomic nuclei">\n        atomic nuclei\n       </a>\n       is often lost in the form of gamma rays when the nuclei are formed, leaving\n       <a href="/wiki/Nuclide" title="Nuclide">\n        nuclides\n       </a>\n       which have less mass than the free particles (\n       <a href="/wiki/Nucleon" title="Nucleon">\n        nucleons\n       </a>\n       ) of which they are composed.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       <a href="/wiki/Mass%E2%80%93energy_equivalence" title="Mass\xe2\x80\x93energy equivalence">\n        Mass\xe2\x80\x93energy equivalence\n       </a>\n       also holds in macroscopic systems.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40">\n        <a href="#cite_note-40">\n         [31]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       For example, if one takes exactly one kilogram of ice, and applies heat, the mass of the resulting melt-water will be more than a kilogram: it will include the mass from the\n       <a href="/wiki/Thermal_energy" title="Thermal energy">\n        thermal energy\n       </a>\n       (\n       <a href="/wiki/Latent_heat" title="Latent heat">\n        latent heat\n       </a>\n       ) used to melt the ice; this follows from the\n       <a href="/wiki/Conservation_of_energy" title="Conservation of energy">\n        conservation of energy\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hecht_41-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-hecht-41">\n         [32]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       This number is small but not negligible: about 3.7 nanograms. It is given by the\n       <a href="/wiki/Latent_heat" title="Latent heat">\n        latent heat\n       </a>\n       of melting ice (334 kJ/kg) divided by the speed of light squared (\n       <i>\n        c\n       </i>\n       <sup>\n        2\n       </sup>\n       = 9\xc3\x9710\n       <sup>\n        16\n       </sup>\n       m\n       <sup>\n        2\n       </sup>\n       /s\n       <sup>\n        2\n       </sup>\n       ).\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="General_relativity">\n        General relativity\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Mass&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: General relativity">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/Mass_in_general_relativity" title="Mass in general relativity">\n        Mass in general relativity\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       In\n       <a href="/wiki/General_relativity" title="General relativity">\n        general relativity\n       </a>\n       , the\n       <a href="/wiki/Equivalence_principle" title="Equivalence principle">\n        equivalence principle\n       </a>\n       is any of several related concepts dealing with the equivalence of\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gravitational_mass" title="Gravitational mass">\n        gravitational\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Inertial_mass" title="Inertial mass">\n        inertial mass\n       </a>\n       . At the core of this assertion is\n       <a href="/wiki/Albert_Einstein" title="Albert Einstein">\n        Albert Einstein\'s\n       </a>\n       idea that the gravitational force as experienced locally while standing on a massive body (such as the Earth) is the same as the\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Fictitious_force" title="Fictitious force">\n         pseudo-force\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       experienced by an observer in a non-\n       <a href="/wiki/Inertial_frame_of_reference" title="Inertial frame of reference">\n        inertial\n       </a>\n       (i.e. accelerated) frame of reference.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       However, it turns out that it is impossible to find an objective general definition for the concept of\n       <a href="/wiki/Invariant_mass" title="Invariant mass">\n        invariant mass\n       </a>\n       in general relativity. At the core of the problem is the\n       <a href="/wiki/Nonlinear_system" title="Nonlinear system">\n        non-linearity\n       </a>\n       of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Einstein_field_equations" title="Einstein field equations">\n        Einstein field equations\n       </a>\n       , making it impossible to write the gravitational field energy as part of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Stress%E2%80%93energy_tensor" title="Stress\xe2\x80\x93energy tensor">\n        stress\xe2\x80\x93energy tensor\n       </a>\n       in a way that is invariant for all observers. For a given observer, this can be achieved by the\n       <a href="/wiki/Stress%E2%80%93energy%E2%80%93momentum_pseudotensor" title="Stress\xe2\x80\x93energy\xe2\x80\x93momentum pseudotensor">\n        stress\xe2\x80\x93energy\xe2\x80\x93momentum pseudotensor\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42">\n        <a href="#cite_note-42">\n         [33]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Mass_in_quantum_physics">\n        Mass in quantum physics\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Mass&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Mass in quantum physics">\n         edit\n mechanics">\n        classical mechanics\n       </a>\n       , the inert mass of a particle appears in the\n       <a href="/wiki/Euler%E2%80%93Lagrange_equation" title="Euler\xe2\x80\x93Lagrange equation">\n        Euler\xe2\x80\x93Lagrange equation\n       </a>\n       as a parameter\n       <i>\n        m\n       </i>\n       :\n      </p>\n      <dl>\n       <dd>\n        <span  <mi mathvariant="normal">\n                   \xe2\x88\x82\n                   <!-- \xe2\x88\x82 -->\n                  </mi>\n                  <mi>\n                   L\n                  </mi>\n       </dd>\n      </dl>\n      <p>\n       After quantization, replacing the position vector\n       <i>\n        x\n       </i>\n       with a\n       <a href="/wiki/Wave_function" title="Wave function">\n        wave function\n       </a>\n       , the parameter\n       <i>\n        m\n       </i>\n       appears in the\n       <a href="/wiki/Kinetic_energy" title="Kinetic energy">\n    </mspace>\n              <mi>\n               t\n              </mi>\n              <mo stretchy="false">\n               )\n              </mo>\n              <mo>\n               =\n              </mo>\n              <mrow>\n               <mo>\n                (\n               </mo>\n               <mo>\n                \xe2\x88\x92\n                <!-- \xe2\x88\x92 -->\n               </mo>\n               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n                <mfrac>\n                 <msup>\n                  <mi class="MJX-variant">\n                   \xe2\x84\x8f\n                   <!-- \xe2\x84\x8f -->\n                  </mi>\n                  <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n                   <mn>\n                    2\n                   </mn>\n                  </mrow>\n                 </msup>\n                 <mrow>\n                  <mn>\n                   2\n                  </mn>\n                  <mi>\n                   m\n                  </mi>\n                 </mrow>\n                </mfrac>\n               </mrow>\n               <msup>\n                <mi mathvariant="normal">\n                 \xe2\x88\x87\n                 <!-- \xe2\x88\x87 -->\n                </mi>\n                <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n                 <mn>\n                  2\n                 </mn>\n                </mrow>\n               </msup>\n               <mo>\n                +\n               </mo>\n               <mi>\n                V\n               </mi>\n               <mo stretchy="false">\n                (\n               </mo>\n               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n                <mi mathvariant="bold">\n                 r\n                </mi>\n               </mrow>\n               <mo stretchy="false">\n                )\n               </mo>\n               <mo>\n                )\n               </mo>\n              </mrow>\n              <mi mathvariant="normal">\n               \xce\xa8\n               <!-- \xce\xa8 -->\n              </mi>\n              <mo stretchy="false">\n               (\n              </mo>\n              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n               <mi mathvariant="bold">\n                r\n               </mi>\n              </mrow>\n              <mo>\n               ,\n              </mo>\n              <mspace width="thinmathspace">\n              </mspace>\n              <mi>\n               t\n              </mi>\n              <mo stretchy="false">\n               )\n              </mo>\n             </mstyle>\n            </mrow>\n            <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\n             {\\displaystyle i\\hbar {\\frac {\\partial }{\\partial t}}\\Psi (\\mathbf {r} ,\\,t)=\\left(-{\\frac {\\hbar ^{2}}{2m}}\\nabla ^{2}+V(\\mathbf {r} (\\mathbf {r} ,\\,t)=\\left(-{\\frac {\\hbar ^{2}}{2m}}\\nabla ^{2}+V(\\mathbf {r} )\\right)\\Psi (\\mathbf {r} ,\\,t)" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/4e77e2d4024342900f85d4f9a1157083e41d6398" style="vertical-align: -2.505ex; width:42.646ex; height:6.343ex;"/>\n        </span>\n        .\n       </dd>\n      </dl>\n      <p>\n       In the ostensibly\n       <a href="/wiki/Covariance_and_contravariance_of_vectors#Informal_usage" title="Covariance and contravariance of vectors">\n        covariant\n       </a>\n       (relativistically invariant)\n       <a href="/wiki/Dirac_equation" title="Dirac equation">\n        Dirac equation\n       </a>\n       , and in\n       <a href="/wiki/Natural_units" title="Natural units">\n        natural units\n       </a>\n       , this becomes:\n      </p>\n      <dl>\n       <dd>\n        <span class="mwe-math-element">\n         <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">\n          <math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n           <semantics>\n            <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n             <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n              <mo stretchy="false">\n               (\n              </mo>\n              <mo>\n               \xe2\x88\x92\n               <!-- \xe2\x88\x92 -->\n              </mo>\n              <mi>\n               i\n              </mi>\n              <msup>\n               <mi>\n                \xce\xb3\n                <!-- \xce\xb3 -->\n               </mi>\n               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n                <mi>\n                 \xce\xbc\n                 <!-- \xce\xbc -->\n                </mi>\n               </mrow>\n              </msup>\n              <msub>\n               <mi mathvariant="normal">\n                \xe2\x88\x82\n                <!-- \xe2\x88\x82 -->\n               </mi>\n               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n                <mi>\n                 \xce\xbc\n                 <!-- \xce\xbc -->\n                </mi>\n               </mrow>\n              </msub>\n              <mo>\n               +\n              </mo>\n              <mi>\n               m\n              </mi>\n              <mo stretchy="false">\n               )\n              </mo>\n              <mi>\n               \xcf\x88\n               <!-- \xcf\x88 -->\n              </mi>\n              <mo>\n               =\n              </mo>\n              <mn>\n               0\n              </mn>\n              <mspace width="thinmathspace">\n              </mspace>\n             </mstyle>\n            </mrow>\n            <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\n             {\\displaystyle (-i\\gamma ^{\\mu }\\partial _{\\mu }+m)\\psi =0\\,}\n            </annotation>\n           </semantics>\n          </math>\n         </span>\n         <img alt="(-i\\gamma ^{\\mu }\\partial _{\\mu }+m)\\psi =0\\," aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/dca46b6bfb51452870cbaeee2359d4b6ca7e1468" style="vertical-align: -1.005ex; width:20.553ex; height:3.009ex;"/>\n        </span>\n       </dd>\n      </dl>\n      <p>\n       where the "\n       <a href="/wiki/Invariant_mass" title="Invariant mass">\n        mass\n       </a>\n       " parameter\n       <i>\n        m\n       </i>\n       is now simply a constant associated with the\n       <a href="/wiki/Quantum" title="Quantum">\n        quantum\n       </a>\n       described by the wave function \xcf\x88.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In the\n       <a href="/wiki/Standard_Model" title="Standard Model">\n        Standard Model\n       </a>\n       of\n       <a href="/wiki/Particle_physics" title="Particle physics">\n        particle physics\n       </a>\n       as developed in the 1960s, this term arises from the coupling of the field \xcf\x88 to an additional field \xce\xa6, the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Higgs_field" title="Higgs field">\n        Higgs field\n       </a>\n       . In the case of fermions, the\n       <a href="/wiki/Higgs_mechanism" title="Higgs mechanism">\n        Higgs mechanism\n       </a>\n       results in the replacement of the term\n       <i>\n        m\n       </i>\n       \xcf\x88 in the Lagrangian with\n       <span class="mwe-math-element">\n        <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">\n         <math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n          <semantics>\n           <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n            <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n             <msub>\n              <mi>\n               G\n              </mi>\n              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n               <mi>\n                \xcf\x88\n                <!-- \xcf\x88 -->\n               </mi>\n              </mrow>\n             </msub>\n             <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n              <mover>\n               <mi>\n                \xcf\x88\n                <!-- \xcf\x88 -->\n               </mi>\n               <mo accent="false">\n                \xc2\xaf\n                <!-- \xc2\xaf -->\n               </mo>\n              </mover>\n             </mrow>\n             <mi>\n              \xcf\x95\n              <!-- \xcf\x95 -->\n             </mi>\n             <mi>\n              \xcf\x88\n              <!-- \xcf\x88 -->\n             </mi>\n            </mstyle>\n           </mrow>\n           <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\n            {\\displaystyle G_{\\psi }{\\overline {\\psi }}\\phi \\psi }\n           </annotation>\n          </semantics>\n         </math>\n        </span>\n        <img alt="G_{\\psi }{\\overline {\\psi }}\\phi \\psi " aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/274591874f17a83bbec652eff5d1cc489bdd839c" style="vertical-align: -1.005ex; width:7.705ex; height:3.676ex;"/>\n       </span>\n       . This shifts the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Explanandum" title="Explanandum">\n        explanandum\n       </a>\n       of the value for the mass of each elementary particle to the value of the unknown couplings\n       <i>\n        G\n       </i>\n       <sub>\n        \xcf\x88\n       </sub>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span id="Tachyonic_particles_and_imaginary_(complex)_mass">\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Tachyonic_particles_and_imaginary_.28complex.29_mass">\n        Tachyonic particles and imaginary (complex) mass\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Mass&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Tachyonic particles and imaginary (complex) mass">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main articles:\n       <a href="/wiki/Tachyonic_field" title="Tachyonic field">\n        Tachyonic field\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Tachyon#Mass" title="Tachyon">\n        Tachyon \xc2\xa7\xc2\xa0Mass\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       A\n       <a href="/wiki/Tachyonic_field" title="Tachyonic field">\n        tachyonic field\n       </a>\n       , or simply\n       <a href="/wiki/Tachyon" title="Tachyon">\n        tachyon\n       </a>\n       , is a\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Quantum_field" title="Quantum field">\n        quantum field\n       </a>\n       with an\n       <a href="/wiki/Imaginary_number" title="Imaginary number">\n        imaginary\n       </a>\n       mass.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Randall_43-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Randall-43">\n         [34]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Although\n       <a href="/wiki/Tachyon" title="Tachyon">\n        tachyons\n       </a>\n       (\n       <a href="/wiki/Particle" title="Particle">\n        particles\n       </a>\n       that move\n       <a href="/wiki/Faster-than-light" title="Faster-than-light">\n        faster than light\n       </a>\n       ) are a purely hypothetical concept not generally believed to exist,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Randall_43-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Randall-43">\n         [34]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tipler_44-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Tipler-44">\n         [35]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <a href="/wiki/Field_(physics)" title="Field (physics)">\n        fields\n       </a>\n       with imaginary mass have come to play an important\n       <a href="/wiki/Higgs_boson" title="Higgs boson">\n        role\n       </a>\n       in modern physics\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kutasov_45-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Kutasov-45">\n         [36]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kutasov_45-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Kutasov-45">\n         [36]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sen_46-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Sen-46">\n         [37]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gibbons_47-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Gibbons-47">\n         [38]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and are discussed in popular books on physics.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Randall_43-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Randall-43">\n         [34]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Greene_48-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Greene-48">\n         [39]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Under no circumstances do any excitations ever propagate faster than light in such theories \xe2\x80\x93 the presence or absence of a tachyonic mass has no effect whatsoever on the maximum velocity of signals (there is no violation of\n       <a href="/wiki/Causality" title="Causality">\n        causality\n       </a>\n       ).\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-susskind_49-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-susskind-49">\n         [40]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       While the\n       <i>\n        field\n       </i>\n       may have imaginary mass, any physical particles do not; the "imaginary mass" shows that the system becomes unstable, and sheds the instability by undergoing a type of\n       <a href="/wiki/Phase_transition" title="Phase transition">\n        phase transition\n       </a>\n       called\n       <a href="/wiki/Tachyon_condensation" title="Tachyon condensation">\n        tachyon condensation\n       </a>\n       (closely related to second order phase transitions) that results in\n       <a href="/wiki/Symmetry_breaking" title="Symmetry breaking">\n        symmetry breaking\n       </a>\n       in\n       <a href="/wiki/Standard_Model" title="Standard Model">\n        current models\n       </a>\n       of\n       <a href="/wiki/Particle_physics" title="Particle physics">\n        particle physics\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The term "\n       <a href="/wiki/Tachyon" title="Tachyon">\n        tachyon\n       </a>\n       " was coined by\n       <a href="/wiki/Gerald_Feinberg" title="Gerald Feinberg">\n        Gerald Feinberg\n       </a>\n       in a 1967 paper,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-feinberg67_50-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-feinberg67-50">\n         [41]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       but it was soon realized that Feinberg\'s model in fact did not allow for\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Superluminal" title="Superluminal">\n        superluminal\n       </a>\n       speeds.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-susskind_49-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-susskind-49">\n         [40]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Instead, the imaginary mass creates an instability in the configuration:- any configuration in which one or more field excitations are tachyonic will spontaneously decay, and the resulting configuration contains no physical tachyons. This process is known as tachyon condensation. Well known examples include the\n       <a href="/wiki/Higgs_mechanism" title="Higgs mechanism">\n        condensation\n       </a>\n       of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Higgs_boson" title="Higgs boson">\n        Higgs boson\n       </a>\n       in\n       <a href="/wiki/Particle_physics" title="Particle physics">\n        particle physics\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Ferromagnetism" title="Ferromagnetism">\n        ferromagnetism\n       </a>\n       in\n       <a href="/wiki/Condensed_matter_physics" title="Condensed matter physics">\n        condensed matter physics\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Although the notion of a tachyonic\n       <a href="/wiki/Imaginary_number" title="Imaginary number">\n        imaginary\n       </a>\n       mass might seem troubling because there is no classical interpretation of an imaginary mass, the mass is not quantized. Rather, the\n       <a href="/wiki/Scalar_field" title="Scalar field">\n        scalar field\n       </a>\n       is; even for tachyonic\n       <a href="/wiki/Quantum_field_theory" title="Quantum field theory">\n        quantum fields\n       </a>\n       , the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Field_operator" title="Field operator">\n        field operators\n       </a>\n       at\n       <a href="/wiki/Minkowski_space" title="Minkowski space">\n        spacelike\n       </a>\n       separated points still\n       <a href="/wiki/Canonical_commutation_relation" title="Canonical commutation relation">\n        commute (or anticommute)\n       </a>\n       , thus preserving causality. Therefore, information still does not propagate faster than light,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-feinberg67_50-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-feinberg67-50">\n         [41]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and solutions grow exponentially, but not superluminally (there is no violation of\n       <a href="/wiki/Causality" title="Causality">\n        causality\n       </a>\n       ).\n       <a href="/wiki/Tachyon_condensation" title="Tachyon condensation">\n        Tachyon condensation\n       </a>\n       drives a physical system that has reached a local limit and might naively be expected to produce physical tachyons, to an alternate stable state where no physical tachyons exist. Once the tachyonic field reaches the minimum of the potential, its quanta are not tachyons any more but rather are ordinary particles with a positive mass-squared.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Peskin_51-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Peskin-51">\n         [42]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       This is a special case of the general rule, where unstable massive particles are formally described as having a\n       <a href="/wiki/Complex_number" title="Complex number">\n        complex\n       </a>\n       mass, with the real part being their mass in the usual sense, and the imaginary part being the\n       <a href="/wiki/Particle_decay#Decay_rate" title="Particle decay">\n        decay rate\n       </a>\n       in\n       <a href="/wiki/Natural_units" title="Natural units">\n        natural units\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Peskin_51-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Peskin-51">\n         [42]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       However, in\n       <a href="/wiki/Quantum_field_theory" title="Quantum field theory">\n        quantum field theory\n       </a>\n       , a particle (a "one-particle state") is roughly defined as a state which is constant over time; i.e., an\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eigenvalue" title="Eigenvalue">\n        eigenvalue\n       </a>\n       of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Hamiltonian_(quantum_mechanics)" title="Hamiltonian (quantum mechanics)">\n        Hamiltonian\n       </a>\n       . An\n       <a href="/wiki/Particle_decay" title="Particle decay">\n        unstable particle\n       </a>\n       is a state which is only approximately constant over time; If it exists long enough to be measured, it can be formally described as having a complex mass, with the real part of the mass greater than its imaginary part. If both parts are of the same magnitude, this is interpreted as a\n       <a href="/wiki/Resonance" title="Resonance">\n        resonance\n       </a>\n       appearing in a scattering process rather than a particle, as it is considered not to exist long enough to be measured independently of the scattering process. In the case of a tachyon the real part of the mass is zero, and hence no concept of a particle can be attributed to it.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In a\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lorentz_invariant" title="Lorentz invariant">\n        Lorentz invariant\n       </a>\n       theory, the same formulas that apply to ordinary slower-than-light particles (sometimes called "\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bradyon" title="Bradyon">\n        bradyons\n       </a>\n       " in discussions of tachyons) must also apply to tachyons. In particular the\n       <a href="/wiki/Energy%E2%80%93momentum_relation" title="Energy\xe2\x80\x93momentum relation">\n        energy\xe2\x80\x93momentum relation\n       </a>\n       :\n      </p>\n      <dl>\n       <dd>\n        <span class="mwe-math-element">\n         <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">\n          <math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n           <semantics>\n            <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n             <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n              <msup>\n               <mi>\n                E\n               </mi>\n               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n                <mn>\n                 2\n                </mn>\n               </mrow>\n              </msup>\n              <mo>\n               =\n              </mo>\n              <msup>\n               <mi>\n                p\n               </mi>\n               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n                <mn>\n                 2\n                </mn>\n               </mrow>\n              </msup>\n              <msup>\n               <mi>\n                c\n               </mi>\n               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n                <mn>\n                 2\n                </mn>\n               </mrow>\n              </msup>\n              <mo>\n               +\n              </mo>\n              <msup>\n               <mi>\n                m\n               </mi>\n               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n                <mn>\n                 2\n                </mn>\n               </mrow>\n              </msup>\n              <msup>\n               <mi>\n                c\n               </mi>\n               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n                <mn>\n                 4\n                </mn>\n               </mrow>\n              </msup>\n              <mspace width="thickmathspace">\n              </mspace>\n             </mstyle>\n            </mrow>\n            <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\n             {\\displaystyle E^{2}=p^{2}c^{2}+m^{2}c^{4}\\;}\n            </annotation>\n           </semantics>\n          </math>\n         </span>\n         <img alt="E^{2}=p^{2}c^{2}+m^{2}c^{4}\\;" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/378fb70d1c7581c9a5c55975a5557f12a5dad121" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:18.983ex; height:3.009ex;"/>\n        </span>\n       </dd>\n      </dl>\n      <p>\n       (where\n       <b>\n        p\n       </b>\n       is the relativistic\n       <a href="/wiki/Momentum" title="Momentum">\n        momentum\n       </a>\n       of the bradyon and\n       <b>\n        m\n       </b>\n       is its\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rest_mass" title="Rest mass">\n        rest mass\n       </a>\n       ) should still apply, along with the formula for the total energy of a particle:\n      </p>\n      <dl>\n       <dd>\n        <span class="mwe-math-element">\n         <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">\n          <math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n           <semantics>\n            <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n             <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n              <mi>\n               E\n              </mi>\n              <mo>\n               =\n              </mo>\n              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n               <mfrac>\n                <mrow>\n                 <mi>\n                  m\n                 </mi>\n                 <msup>\n                  <mi>\n                   c\n                  </mi>\n                  <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n                   <mn>\n                    2\n                   </mn>\n                  </mrow>\n                 </msup>\n                </mrow>\n                <msqrt>\n                 <mn>\n                  1\n                 </mn>\n                 <mo>\n                  \xe2\x88\x92\n                  <!-- \xe2\x88\x92 -->\n                 </mo>\n                 <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n                  <mfrac>\n                   <msup>\n                    <mi>\n                     v\n                    </mi>\n                    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n                     <mn>\n                      2\n                     </mn>\n                    </mrow>\n                   </msup>\n                   <msup>\n                    <mi>\n                     c\n                    </mi>\n                    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n                     <mn>\n                      2\n                     </mn>\n                    </mrow>\n                   </msup>\n                  </mfrac>\n                 </mrow>\n                </msqrt>\n               </mfrac>\n              </mrow>\n              <mo>\n               .\n              </mo>\n             </mstyle>\n            </mrow>\n            <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\n             {\\displaystyle E={\\frac {mc^{2}}{\\sqrt {1-{\\frac {v^{2}}{c^{2}}}}}}.}\n            </annotation>\n           </semantics>\n          </math>\n         </span>\n         <img alt="E={\\frac {mc^{2}}{\\sqrt {1-{\\frac {v^{2}}{c^{2}}}}}}." aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/724fe90452d2f107f6201a34b05709d7deed4f66" style="vertical-align: -4.671ex; width:15.225ex; height:8.509ex;"/>\n        </span>\n       </dd>\n      </dl>\n      <p>\n       This equation shows that the total energy of a particle (bradyon or tachyon) contains a contribution from its rest mass (the "rest mass\xe2\x80\x93energy") and a contribution from its motion, the kinetic energy. When\n       <i>\n        v\n       </i>\n       is larger than\n       <i>\n        c\n       </i>\n       , the denominator in the equation for the energy is\n       <a href="/wiki/Imaginary_number" title="Imaginary number">\n        "imaginary"\n       </a>\n       , as the value under the\n       <a href="/wiki/Square_root" title="Square root">\n        radical\n       </a>\n       is negative. Because the total\n       <a href="/wiki/Energy" title="Energy">\n        energy\n       </a>\n       must be\n       <a href="/wiki/Real_number" title="Real number">\n        real\n       </a>\n       , the numerator must\n       <i>\n        also\n       </i>\n       be imaginary: i.e. the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rest_mass" title="Rest mass">\n        rest mass\n       </a>\n       <b>\n        m\n       </b>\n       must be imaginary, as a pure imaginary number divided by another pure imaginary number is a real number.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Exotic_matter_and_negative_mass">\n        Exotic matter and negative mass\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Mass&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Exotic matter and negative mass">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/Negative_mass" title="Negative mass">\n        negative mass\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <a href="/wiki/Negative_mass" title="Negative mass">\n        negative mass\n       </a>\n       exists in the model to describe\n       <a href="/wiki/Dark_energy" title="Dark energy">\n        dark energy\n       </a>\n       (\n       <a href="/wiki/Phantom_energy" title="Phantom energy">\n        phantom energy\n       </a>\n       ) and\n       <a href="/wiki/Radiation" title="Radiation">\n        radiation\n       </a>\n       in\n       <a href="/wiki/Negative-index_metamaterial" title="Negative-index metamaterial">\n        negative-index metamaterial\n       </a>\n       in a unified way.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52">\n        <a href="#cite_note-52">\n         [43]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In this way, the negative mass is associated with\n       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Negative_momentum&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Negative momentum (page does not exist)">\n        negative momentum\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Pressure#Negative_pressures" title="Pressure">\n        negative pressure\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Negative_kinetic_energy&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Negative kinetic energy (page does not exist)">\n        negative kinetic energy\n       </a>\n       and FTL (\n       <a href="/wiki/Faster-than-light" title="Faster-than-light">\n        faster-than-light\n       </a>\n       ).\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">\n        See also\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Mass&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: See also">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <ul>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Mass_versus_weight" title="Mass versus weight">\n         Mass versus weight\n        </a>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Effective_mass_(spring%E2%80%93mass_system)" title="Effective mass (spring\xe2\x80\x93mass system)">\n         Effective mass (spring\xe2\x80\x93mass system)\n        </a>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Effective_mass_(solid-state_physics)" title="Effective mass (solid-state physics)">\n         Effective mass (solid-state physics)\n        </a>\n <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">\n        Notes\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Mass&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Notes">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: decimal;">\n       <div class="mw-references-wrap">\n        <ol class="references">\n         <li id="cite_note-3">\n          <span class="mw-cite-backlink">\n           <b>\n            <a href="#cite_ref-3">\n             ^\n            </a>\n           </b>\n          </span>\n          <span class="reference-text">\n           When a distinction is necessary,\n           <i>\n            M\n           </i>\n           is used to denote the active gravitational mass and\n           <i>\n            m\n           </i>\n           the passive gravitational mass.\n          </span>\n         </li>\n         <li id="cite_note-6">\n          <span class="mw-cite-backlink">\n           <b>\n            <a href="#cite_ref-6">\n             ^\n            </a>\n           </b>\n          </span>\n          <span class="reference-text">\n           Since the\n           <a href="/wiki/Avogadro_constant" title="Avogadro constant">\n            Avogadro constant\n           </a>\n           <i>\n            N\n           </i>\n           <sub>\n            A\n           </sub>\n           is defined as the number of atoms in 12\xc2\xa0g of carbon-12, it follows that 1\xc2\xa0u is exactly 1/(10\n           <sup>\n            3\n           </sup>\n           <i>\n            N\n           </i>\n           <sub>\n            A\n           </sub>\n           )\xc2\xa0kg.\n          </span>\n         </li>\n         <li id="cite_note-8">\n          <span class="mw-cite-backlink">\n           <b>\n            <a href="#cite_ref-8">\n             ^\n            </a>\n           </b>\n          </span>\n          <span class="reference-text">\n           The distinction between "active" and "passive" gravitational mass does not exist in the Newtonian view of gravity as found in\n           <a href="/wiki/Classical_mechanics" title="Classical mechanics">\n            classical mechanics\n           </a>\n           , and can safely be ignored for many purposes. In most practical applications, Newtonian gravity is assumed because it is usually sufficiently accurate, and is simpler than General Relativity; for example, NASA uses primarily Newtonian gravity to design space missions, although "accuracies are routinely enhanced by accounting for tiny relativistic effects".\n           <span class="url">\n            <a class="external text" href="http://www2.jpl.nasa.gov/basics/bsf3-2.php" rel="nofollow">\n             www2\n             <wbr/>\n             .jpl\n             <wbr/>\n             .nasa\n             <wbr/>\n             .gov\n             <wbr/>\n             /basics\n             <wbr/>\n             /bsf3-2\n             <wbr/>\n             .php\n            </a>\n           </span>\n           The distinction between "active" and "passive" is very abstract, and applies to post-graduate level applications of General Relativity to certain problems in cosmology, and is otherwise not used. There is, nevertheless, an important conceptual distinction in Newtonian physics between "inertial mass" and "gravitational mass", although these quantities are identical; the conceptual distinction between these two fundamental definitions of mass is maintained for teaching purposes because they involve two distinct methods of measurement. It was long considered anomalous that the two distinct measurements of mass (inertial and gravitational) gave an identical result. The property, observed by Galileo, that objects of different mass fall with the same rate of acceleration (ignoring air resistance), shows that inertial and gravitational mass are the same.\n          </span>\n         </li>\n         <li id="cite_note-13">\n          <span class="mw-cite-backlink">\n           <b>\n            <a href="#cite_ref-13">\n             ^\n            </a>\n           </b>\n          </span>\n          <span class="reference-text">\n           This constant ratio was later shown to be a direct measure of the Sun\'s active gravitational mass; it has units of distance cubed per time squared, and is known as the\n           <a href="/wiki/Standard_gravitational_parameter" title="Standard gravitational parameter">\n            standard gravitational parameter\n           </a>\n           :\n          </span>\n          <dl>\n           <dd>\n            <span class="reference-text">\n             <span class="mwe-math-element">\n              <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">\n               <math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n                <semantics>\n                 <mrow   </mi>\n                   <mo>\n                    =\n                   </mo>\n                   <mn>\n                    4\n                   </mn>\n                   <msup>\n                    <mi>\n                     \xcf\x80\n                     <!-- \xcf\x80 -->\n                    </mi>\n                    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n                     <mn>\n                      2\n                     </mn>\n                    </mrow>\n                   </msup>\n                   <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n                    <mfrac>\n                     <msup>\n                      <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n                       <mtext>\n                        distance\n                       </mtext>\n                      </mrow>\n                      <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n                       <mn>\n                        3\n                       </mn>\n                      </mrow>\n                     </msup>\n                     <msup>\n                      <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n                       <mtext>\n                        time\n                       </mtext>\n                      </mrow>\n                      <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n                       <mn>\n                        2\n                       </mn>\n                      </mrow>\n                     </msup>\n                    </mfrac>\n                   </mrow>\n                   <mo>\n                    \xe2\x88\x9d\n                    <!-- \xe2\x88\x9d -->\n                   </mo>\n                   <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n                    <mtext>\n                     gravitational mass\n                    </mtext>\n                   </mrow>\n                  </mstyle>\n                 </mrow>\n                 <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\n                  {\\displaystyle \\mu =4\\pi ^{2}{\\frac {{\\text{distance}}^{3}}{{\\text{time}}^{2}}}\\propto {\\text{gravitational mass}}}\n                 </annotation>\n                </semantics>\n               </math>\n              </span>\n              <img alt="\\mu =4\\pi ^{2}{\\frac {{\\text{distance}}^{3}}{{\\text{time}}^{2}}}\\propto {\\text{gravitational mass}}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/803742e5257798ecb4ce03a381cc5ff6efac9bb3" style="vertical-align: -2.338ex; width:40.153ex; height:6.343ex;"/>\n             </span>\n            </span>\n           </dd>\n          </dl>\n         </li>\n         <li id="cite_note-15">\n          <span class="mw-cite-backlink">\n           <b>\n            <a href="#cite_ref-15">\n             ^\n            </a>\n           </b>\n          </span>\n          <span class="reference-text">\n           At the time when Viviani asserts that the experiment took place, Galileo had not yet formulated the final version of his law of free fall. He had, however, formulated an earlier version which predicted that bodies\n           <i>\n            of the same material\n           </i>\n           falling through the same medium would fall at the same speed. See\n           <cite class="citation book">\n            Drake, S. (1978).\n            <i>\n             Galileo at Work\n            </i>\n            .\n            <a href="/wiki/University_of_Chicago_Press" title="University of Chicago Press">\n             University of Chicago Press\n            </a>\n            . pp.\xc2\xa019\xe2\x80\x9320.\n            <a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number" title="International Standard Book Number">\n             ISBN\n            </a>\n            <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0-226-16226-5" title="Special:BookSources/0-226-16226-5">\n             0-226-16226-5\n            </a>\n            .\n           </cite>\n           <span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Galileo+at+Work&amp;rft.pages=19-20&amp;rft.pub=University+of+Chicago+Press&amp;rft.date=1978&amp;rft.isbn=0-226-16226-5&amp;rft.aulast=Drake&amp;rft.aufirst=S.&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AMass">\n            <span style="display:none;">\n            </span>\n           </span>\n          </span>\n         </li>\n         <li id="cite_note-24">\n          <span class="mw-cite-backlink">\n           <b>\n            <a href="#cite_ref-24">\n             ^\n            </a>\n           </b>\n          </span>\n          <span class="reference-text">\n           These two properties are very useful, as they allow spherical collections of objects to be treated exactly like large individual objects.\n          </span>\n         </li>\n         <li id="cite_note-29">\n          <span class="mw-cite-backlink">\n           <b>\n            <a href="#cite_ref-29">\n             ^\n            </a>\n           </b>\n          </span>\n          <span class="reference-text">\n           In its original form, Newton\'s second law is valid only for bodies of constant mass.\n          </span>\n         </li>\n         <li id="cite_note-33">\n          <span class="mw-cite-backlink">\n           <b>\n            <a href="#cite_ref-33">\n             ^\n            </a>\n           </b>\n          </span>\n          <span class="reference-text">\n           It is possible to make a slight distinction between "rest mass" and "invariant mass". For a system of two or more particles, none of the particles are required be at rest with respect to the observer for the system as a whole to be at rest with respect to the observer. To avoid this confusion, some sources will use "rest mass" only for individual particles, and "invariant mass" for systems.\n          </span>\n         </li>\n         <li id="cite_note-34">\n          <span class="mw-cite-backlink">\n           <b>\n            <a href="#cite_ref-34">\n             ^\n            </a>\n           </b>\n          </span>\n          <span class="reference-text">\n           For example, a nuclear bomb in an idealized super-strong box, sitting on a scale, would in theory show no change in mass when detonated (although the inside of the box would become much hotter). In such a system, the mass of the box would change only if energy were allowed to escape from the box as light or heat. However, in that case, the removed energy would take its associated mass with it. Letting heat or radiation out of such a system is simply a way to remove mass. Thus, mass, like energy, cannot be destroyed, but only moved from one place to another.\n          </span>\n         </li>\n        </ol>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="References">\n        References\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Mass&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: References">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="reflist columns references-column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 30em; -webkit-column-width: 30em; column-width: 30em; list-style-type: decimal;">\n       <ol class="references">\n        <li id="cite_note-1">\n         <span class="mw-cite-backlink">\n          <b>\n           <a href="#cite_ref-1">\n            ^\n           </a>\n          </b>\n         </span>\n         <span class="reference-text">\n          <a class="external free" href="http://dictionary.reference.com/browse/mass" rel="nofollow">\n           http://dictionary.reference.com/browse/mass\n          </a>\n         </span>\n        </li>\n        <li id="cite_note-2">\n         <span class="mw-cite-backlink">\n          <b>\n           <a href="#cite_ref-2">\n            ^\n           </a>\n          </b>\n         </span>\n         <span class="reference-text">\n          <cite class="citation web">\n           <a class="external text" href="http://www.technologyreview.com/view/419367/new-quantum-theory-separates-gravitational-and-inertial-mass/" rel="nofollow">\n            "New Quantum Theory Separates Gravitational and Inertial Mass"\n           </a>\n           . a\n               </span>\n               \xe2\x80\x93\n               <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">\n                g\n               </span>\n               are algebraic exponents, usually a positive, negative or zero integer.)\n              </small>\n              <br/>\n             </div>\n            </td>\n           </tr>\n           <tr>\n            <th
